He talks about/sees Anna all the time, she has taken up his entire life. Why? They don't even seem like they're in love. In my first review, I said exactly the same thing. The two characters have no buildup with each other and this is insta-love on a whole new level. He hears her name and it's INSTA-LOVE.<br><i>“Anything,” she shrugs. “What’s made her so special? What made you so special to her, that she’d send herself into oblivion for you?” “I don’t know,” I say. Why did I say that? I do know. I knew it the moment I heard Anna’s name, and the first time she spoke.</i> <br> I understand seeing her story would maybe make you <i>like</i> her, but love? No. I feel love needs to be stronger than that, that's what I hope for. Than out of the blue in the first book they're making out and hugging and they barely know anything about each other. ANYWAY! I found the plot for this book weak, but cute. Cas so determined to bring Anna back to him willing to even go to the other side to do it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[only to inevitably set her free it breaks my heart <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>All in all, I like Cas but I didn't like him as much as I did in the first one. I found him and Anna cheesy and unrealistic, but cute and what Cas did was very romantic.<br><br><br><b>Thomas/Carmel</b> Practically both of these characters weren't even characters in this book. You hardly never saw them away from each other. They barely talked. In the beginning, Carmel decides that she doesn't want to do this anymore. She publicly embarrasses Thomas, breaks his heart. Than when he goes to England, she randomly shows up and gets back together with him with no backstory to that all? No reason why she changed her mind? she just shows up and acts like she gives a fuck again? ANNOYING.<br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/get%20out%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/271826.gif" alt="get out Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>Than they get back together and you don't even know why. At all. The next time you see them they're PDA it up. I understand that they are mainly side characters but I think the author should have at least included why. <br>Another thing that bothered me was... Carmel/Thomas were not characters. They had no depth, no story, barely even had conversations. The only "some-what" moment you see Thomas is when he's all sulky. I preferred him in the first book, before Carmel and him were joined to the hip.<br><br><br><b>Plot/Writing</b> The writing with Kendare Blake is always good. Smooth, easy to understand, simple. But, this book bored me. I couldn't wait until I got to the end. I also found the only redeeming quality in this book to be the end. It was sad, heartbreaking, beautifully captured. But the rest of the book bored me to tears. The plot was also very cheesy, I was hoping it'd be more hunting new monsters and a new plot. Not an entire plot centered all on Anna. Don't get me wrong, she was an all right character. I just do not think she should have been the main plot, perhaps a sideplot? I'm not quite sure.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_207228551" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207228551" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207228551?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207228551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2722217277689248393"><br/>In Girl of Nightmares we pick up several months after Anna sacrificed herself to save Cas, Thomas and Carmel, by taking the Obeahman to Hell. Since then, Cas has been going through the motions of life and school. He follows up on ghost tips with Carmel and Thomas tagging along. The three of them now form a sort of ghost-busting team. However, Cas can't get Anna out of his head. Everyone has done research and they've consulted the spiritual community but they can't nail down what happened to Anna</span>
  <span id="freeText2722217277689248393" style="display:none"><br />In Girl of Nightmares we pick up several months after Anna sacrificed herself to save Cas, Thomas and Carmel, by taking the Obeahman to Hell. Since then, Cas has been going through the motions of life and school. He follows up on ghost tips with Carmel and Thomas tagging along. The three of them now form a sort of ghost-busting team. However, Cas can't get Anna out of his head. Everyone has done research and they've consulted the spiritual community but they can't nail down what happened to Anna. Suddenly, Cas starts hearing and seeing Anna all over the place: in the face of another student, through the laugh of another ghost, or just in the middle of his bedroom. If this is really Anna, it's not good because she doesn't appear to have gone to a peaceful place <i>at all</i>. Everyone says it's impossible, that she can't come back, so Cas doesn't know if it's his mind playing tricks on him. Cas sets out to find out if Anna really needs help, it's the least he can do for her now. <br /><br />Overall I enjoyed the conclusion to this story but, in my opinion, it didn't live up to Anna Dressed In Blood. That being said, I still liked it. The creepy and spooky factor that was in Anna, was in this one too. Some of the ghost hunting scenes are spine tingling scary. While we still get our snarky wise-cracking Cas, I feel his personality was a little dampened by his depression over Anna, which I guess is understandable considering his situation. I loved the bits of Thomas and Carmel. These two opposites have a sweet romance that I found to be a highlight in this story. I also liked the new character Jestine, she was tough and bad-ass. The type of girl I love to read about. I think I would've enjoyed this even more if she was more of a prominent character earlier on. We're not even introduced to her until half-way through the story, which is a shame because I saw great potential with her and Cas. <br /><br />One of the reasons I usually shy away from ghost/human romance stories is because, really, how can it end well? So while I felt the ending was fitting, it left me with bittersweet feelings. <br /><br />You can read this review and more on <br /><a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2012/07/review-girl-of-nightmares-by-kendare.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2722217277689248393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer659383172" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10871190541864857637"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413412555i/11507322.jpg' width='236' height='257' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In honour of my favourite holiday of all, <b>Halloween</b>, I am dedicating the month of October to all those things that go bump, bang, boom in the night (and day). <br/><br/>This book is spillover from last year’s impossibly long Spooktober to-read list. Why did it fall by the wayside you may like to know…. (you probably don’t, but I’m telling you anyways.) <br/><br/>I have an issue with loving one book by an author and then feeling less loving towards the rest of their works. And I LOVED <u>Anna Dressed in Blood</u>! That boo</span>
  <span id="freeText10871190541864857637" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413412555i/11507322.jpg" width="236" height="257" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In honour of my favourite holiday of all, <b>Halloween</b>, I am dedicating the month of October to all those things that go bump, bang, boom in the night (and day). <br><br>This book is spillover from last year’s impossibly long Spooktober to-read list. Why did it fall by the wayside you may like to know…. (you probably don’t, but I’m telling you anyways.) <br><br>I have an issue with loving one book by an author and then feeling less loving towards the rest of their works. And I LOVED <u>Anna Dressed in Blood</u>! That book was phenomenal. So little old me got scared, guys, because this is the sequel to a book I <b>love</b>, and I am not much of a sequels girl. I mean, I probably have twenty currently unfinished being read series just sitting there, giving me doe eyes, on my shelf. And the reason is that something always seems to go wrong for me in the follow through of a series. <br><br><u>Girl of Nightmares</u> was VERY good, however I did not love it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445288722i/16624965._SX540_.jpg" width="428" height="321.2" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The real estate between a four star and a five star is SIGNIFICANT for me. So while I would recommend this book as being extremely well executed it’s like having a decent restaurant stew compared to my gramma’s stew (which was LEGEND in my household), it doesn’t really compete with the first. <br><br>I liked that we saw major character development and some hiccups and fissures in existing relationships. The gore elements, once again, were incredibly well done. The fact that Blake essentially altered the landscape between these two books is impressive. More backstory was added, which I love!!! This definitely isn’t stagnation of the first book trying to bleed into a second one. This is a SOLID book, worthy of praise of its own merit. I think this is just a case of my having way too high expectations.<br><br><i>There’s pure silence on the drive from the school to my house. I can’t think of a single thing to say and I feel useless. My lack of experience at friendship is showing. Thomas looks as brittle as a brown leaf. Someone else would know something, some anecdote or story. Someone else would know what to do besides sit in the passenger seat and be uncomfortable.</i><br><br>Cas is terribly endearing. He’s flawed and complete feeling in his voice, that has not changed in this sequel. <br><br>I have one little point I really want to make though, and it’s probably just a me thing: The title, <u>Girl of Nightmares</u> doesn’t feel appropriate. Anna, my favourite character from the first book, has next to no page time in this book; ‘The Boy with the Athame’ would have been much less misleading for me. <br></span>

    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/538343556?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer538343556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9627932729864246009">I had high expectations for this book based on the first. The bar was set so high that I was inevitably let down. I did not like this book much. The creepy crawly is still there; Kendare Blake does creepy like few other authors can, it's just a lot more toned down this time around. I didn't find myself gagging upon reading a description, which is good or bad, depending on one's tastes.<br/><br/>Cal is getting over the loss of his ghostly love, and seeing her when he shouldn't. Of course, all his friends t</span>
  <span id="freeText9627932729864246009" style="display:none">I had high expectations for this book based on the first. The bar was set so high that I was inevitably let down. I did not like this book much. The creepy crawly is still there; Kendare Blake does creepy like few other authors can, it's just a lot more toned down this time around. I didn't find myself gagging upon reading a description, which is good or bad, depending on one's tastes.<br /><br />Cal is getting over the loss of his ghostly love, and seeing her when he shouldn't. Of course, all his friends thinks he's nuts. He is completely broken, going through his day like a zombie, much to the worry of Carmel and Thomas. Carmel and Thomas, now there is the two bright points in this book. Their relationship evolves, they grow into characters with their own thoughts and behavior, and they struggle. Man, I loved the two of them in this book.<br /><br />Cas was just boring and annoying, I missed the old cocky son of a bitch attitude he has in <i>Anna Dressed in Blood</i>. In this book, I just wanted to slap him and tell him to wake the f*** up. Remember how Bella was when Edward left her? God, that was a terrible book, but that was exactly how I felt Cas was acting.<br /><br />There's little action besides moping and whining for most of the novel. New characters are introduced, the majority of whom I hate. Even with its faults, I'd still rather read this book than 90% of the YA supernatural fiction out there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9627932729864246009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_211594574" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/211594574" />
    <a title="Anzu The Great Destroyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer"><img alt="Anzu The Great Destroyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455829739p2/2278800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/211594574?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anzu The Great Destroyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anzu The Great Destroyer" href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer">Anzu The Great Destroyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13519280-girl-of-nightmares">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=ya-is-dead">ya-is-dead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=ghests">ghests</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=d-oh">d-oh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=fat-kitty-judges-you">fat-kitty-judges-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=i-am-disappoint">i-am-disappoint</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=zzzzzzz">zzzzzzz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=facepalm">facepalm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=excitement">excitement</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=dafuq-did-i-just-read">dafuq-did-i-just-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=meh-just-ok">meh-just-ok</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer211594574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7672767718977088199"><blockquote>
  <b>“Cassio,” she whispers. “Get me out of here.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Girl of Nightmares</i> starts with Anna being gone. Remember the previous book? The whole jump straight into a fiery pit thing? Anyhow, it’s beet months since the little “accident," and Cas can’t stop obsessing over her. He hears her laugh and sees her, or things that remind him of her, everywhere he goes. He can’t focus on his ghost killing job. School sucks, and his friends can’t seem to stand him because of his douchey attitude. No surprise there.<br/><br/>C</span>
  <span id="freeText7672767718977088199" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>“Cassio,” she whispers. “Get me out of here.”</b>
</blockquote><br><i>Girl of Nightmares</i> starts with Anna being gone. Remember the previous book? The whole jump straight into a fiery pit thing? Anyhow, it’s beet months since the little “accident," and Cas can’t stop obsessing over her. He hears her laugh and sees her, or things that remind him of her, everywhere he goes. He can’t focus on his ghost killing job. School sucks, and his friends can’t seem to stand him because of his douchey attitude. No surprise there.<br><br>Cas also can’t stop trying to get himself killed. Ok, maybe he’s not <i>trying</i> to get himself killed, but he’s not doing a good job staying away from trouble either. All of this is in the name of love! He will stop at nothing in order to get Anna back into the world of the living. Even though, you know, she’s dead and all.<br><br>I could tell there’s something fishy going on with <i>Girl of Nightmares</i> since page one. First of all, it did not suck me in since the beginning like <i>Anna Dressed in Blood</i> had and secondly, I could tell that it was obviously different than the previous installment. <br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359424i/710460._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My main problem regarding the book is Cas. He seems to have been replaced with a bitter old man. Yes, I know that it could be understandable. He lost his lover girl. He is suffering. He is constantly moping over Anna. Boo-hoo. However, this is not a decent enough reason to get on my nerves and ruin a perfectly good book. If only <i>Girl of Nightmares</i> <i>was</i> a perfectly good book, that is.<br><br>I liked the first book, <i>Anna Dressed in Blood</i>, and I was ok with the romance that was going on between Cas and Anna. Now, it’s been a year, give or take, since I read it, and I’m starting to have different thoughts about the two “lovebirds." The whole “I miss you, and I might just love you” part seems a bit unhealthy for Cas.<br><br>I mean, ok, hooking up with a ghost. Good luck getting to second base with that. But a ghost that is capable of mutilating people? And is full of blood, stab wounds and gore most of the time. Well, I think one would need a strong stomach even to think about going to second base with her. Just sayin’.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“ […] in the third chair in, Anna winks at me. Or maybe she just blinks. I can’t tell. She’s missing half of her face. </b>
</blockquote><br>I mean come on. You’re still starry-eyed after this? Earth to Cas. She’s missing half of her fucking face. Just scream and hide under the desk already.<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380359424ra/710461.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Let’s pretend this never happened.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Anna is waiting in my bedroom. Her head lolls as if on a broken neck; her eyes roll up to mine. </b>
</blockquote><br>Cas , don’t you feel like kissing her? Not even a little bit?<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“I don’t try to read her lips. Too much black blood spills through them. </b>
</blockquote><br>He’s so going to make out with her right now. His girlfriend. Ghost girlfriend. Someone’s going to die a virgin. I think the moral of this story is: <i>love prevails over all</i>. Or something.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“ “I love her.” <br>“She’s dead.” <br>“That doesn’t mean to me what it does to other people.” </b>
</blockquote><br>That means you’re having a shitload of problems coming your way, kid.<br><br>Do you see what I’m talking about? How can I even remotely like this book with all this nonsense going on? <br><br><u>A short conclusion</u><br>I admit I don’t have the best memory out there. This means that I don’t remember much from <i>Anna Dressed in Blood</i>. I do remember the main events but not the little details. However, the thing that impressed me the most in <i>Anna Dressed in Blood</i> were the terrifying ghosts, carnage and the environment's overall dark and chilling feel. All these elements are absent in <i>Girl of Nightmares</i>, which reads more like teenage angst slash romance than horror. This is a very sad thing because Kendare Blake has a good talent in creating amazing horror concepts. I am extremely disappointed.<br><br><u>Favorite quote:</u><br><blockquote>
  <b>“She’ll see her dressed in blood, her hair floating like it’s suspended in water, eyes black and shining. And when she does, she won’t be able to catch her breath. </b>
</blockquote><br>P.S. I’m still waiting for the real Anna #2 to come out. This one was probably just an April’s Fool joke.<br><br>Barely 3 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7672767718977088199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1977085398?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=paranormal-urban-fantasy">paranormal-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=witches-magicians">witches-magicians</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1977085398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8713532096227587455"><b>*3.5/5 where-the-hell-are-half-stars-when-one-needs-them-this-badly stars*</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>“Every time I question him about the feasibility, he smiles at me like he's Yoda and I'm just a dumbass without the Force.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>This book wrecked me! It wasn't as great as the first book - the first half dragged a bit, there simply wasn't enough ghost hunting as in the first one <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[and lets just say that Jestine is not my favourite character on this planet <i>*whispers* *so annoying*</i> <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - and while the</span>
  <span id="freeText8713532096227587455" style="display:none"><b>*3.5/5 where-the-hell-are-half-stars-when-one-needs-them-this-badly stars*</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Every time I question him about the feasibility, he smiles at me like he's Yoda and I'm just a dumbass without the Force.”</b>
</i><br /><br />This book wrecked me! It wasn't as great as the first book - the first half dragged a bit, there simply wasn't enough ghost hunting as in the first one <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and lets just say that Jestine is not my favourite character on this planet <i>*whispers* *so annoying*</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - and while the ending is meaningful and perfect way to end this duology, I'm not sure it's entirely for me. Don't get me wrong, it had me emotional all over the place and I did love it, but it's bittersweet adventure for sure. Also side note: where the hell was Anna for like 99% of this book? There was not enough of her! I was sad that she wasn't a major character here. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“I don't care what your name is," she hisses. "And I don't care who you are. If you don't get him some help, I will burn your fucking place down." Go Carmel.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The very last part - mostly the last few chapters - was such a kick-ass, gruesome adventure and I loved it to pieces. This book wasn't perfect, yet it really affected me in many ways. Even though I rated it one star less, it's still highly recommended read for those who enjoyed <i>Anna Dressed in Blood</i>.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Cassio,” she whispers. “Get me out of here.”</i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_732165706" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/732165706" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/732165706?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=writing-envy">writing-envy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=kick-ass-character">kick-ass-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer732165706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16658226869001849317">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Now this is, ladies and gentlemen is what YA humorous horror is all about. This was the one, and only sequel to Anna Dressed in Blood. And I don't think it could have been more flawless. <br/><br/>Ever since the savage ghost Anna disappeared into Hell, Cas- a ghost hunter thought he would be able to move on, forget the girl that caught his heart. Yet as each day passes, it's never getting easier. It's like Anna is still there, haunting Cas. And she is. But why</span>
  <span id="freeText16658226869001849317" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br /><br /><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />Now this is, ladies and gentlemen is what YA humorous horror is all about. This was the one, and only sequel to Anna Dressed in Blood. And I don't think it could have been more flawless. <br /><br />Ever since the savage ghost Anna disappeared into Hell, Cas- a ghost hunter thought he would be able to move on, forget the girl that caught his heart. Yet as each day passes, it's never getting easier. It's like Anna is still there, haunting Cas. And she is. But why? In Girl of Nightmares, we are reintroduced to our amazing cast, along with a few more characters. However, unlike Anna Dressed in Blood- where Anna was the main spotlight, Cas is the one here. He's haunted, lost and in despair. He still cannot live one day without Anna on his mind. And with her seeming to be haunting him, reaching for his help, the situations don't get better. However! we still have plenty of his sarcastic humour, he isn't full on in sadness and regret. I have always been a fan of his snark in his inner dialogue. A highly likeable male protagonist. <br /><br />We do get more friendship building between Cas, Carmel and Thomas. (Maybe even a romance between Carmel and Thomas! Eep) Carmel became fairly distant in this book, we start to discover early on she's hiding something. And seems rather uncomfortable at the same time. As for Thomas, he's our sweet nerdy guy with a lot of bravery than you'd expect. This trio of friendshipiness has to be one of my favourite friendships ever. All have some level of badassery. Alas, the main un-perfection in Girl of Nightmares was Anna. We barely encounter her real self until sometime later which did make me begin to think the pace could have been a little faster. Not to state that it was incredibly lagging and boring- HELL NO but I would have appreciated more of Anna and if the pace got through most of the book, and stretched the last bit a little more, I would have been more satisfied. <br /><br />Kendare Blake's writing does not get enough praises. I love it. I love it. I love it! The quick switches between gloom and snark, horror and sweet is absolutely amazing and I have a writing envy. All the descriptions and scenes were topped perfectly with a sprinkle of gruesomeness.<br /><br />And the ending was completely satisfying. I really did hope deep down that this was the way it ended and it did and I was just doing a little happy dance inside. I cannot recommend this series enough! If you want some light horror with a dose of humorous and kick-ass characters AND some witty writing, the Anna series should be the first series to look for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16658226869001849317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_490734453" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/490734453" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/490734453?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=ebook_nook">ebook_nook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=multi-dimensional">multi-dimensional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=romance-y">romance-y</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer490734453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1828860714223426160">Ugh. This will be a rant... Just warning you ahead of time.<br/><br/>Seriously, I'm pretty annoyed right now. I just finished Girl of Nightmares, and I'm really wondering why Kendare Blake went the New Moon direction with the story rather than the rather more interesting and meaningful and purposeful "Let's save my Dad" direction. Because she could have, easily, and it would have been a better story for it. <br/><br/>I mean, this duology had the potential to be amazing. Book one was almost there, but the stupid rom</span>
  <span id="freeText1828860714223426160" style="display:none">Ugh. This will be a rant... Just warning you ahead of time.<br><br>Seriously, I'm pretty annoyed right now. I just finished Girl of Nightmares, and I'm really wondering why Kendare Blake went the New Moon direction with the story rather than the rather more interesting and meaningful and purposeful "Let's save my Dad" direction. Because she could have, easily, and it would have been a better story for it. <br><br>I mean, this duology had the potential to be amazing. Book one was almost there, but the stupid romance instant connection THAT I STILL DON'T GET AND WAS COMPLETELY POINTLESS (other than making me want to throatpunch the main character every 3 or 4 pages), and it sapped the awesome right out. <br><br>Book two started with that awesome-deficient romance-y, mopey, ghost-longing shell of a story, and then proceeded to stab it repeatedly with the plot line from New Moon. Which, I mean, is less a stab than a kind of wet and pathetic flopping, but you catch my drift, right? <br><br>At one point, I was calling the main character Casbella. Because that's pretty much how I thought of Cas in this book. He was no longer the witty, sarcastic teen from book one... now he's a mopey little bitch who can't explain why he loves or is drawn to Anna but he JUST IS! GAH! CAN'T YOU UNDER<i>STAND</i> THAT?! *foot stomp* <br><br>Nevermind the fact that she's dead. Nevermind the fact that they spent less than 9 months "together". Nevermind that they have nothing in common except an unwillingness to change their clothes. They are in lurrrrrrve. So Cas needs to save her from the awful meaniepoopoohead that oh yeah... alsohappenedtokillCas'sfather... if we want to be specific. But he's PICKING on ANNA! *stomps foot*<br><br>I can't even begin to generate enough angst to impersonate Cas. Because there isn't enough in my body... or even my neighborhood. And there's a school two blocks away. <br><br>*deep breath* <br><br>OK. Before, I said that this could have been a better story if Blake had gone in a different direction with it. Lemme 'splain why I feel that way. First, some points: <br>1) the Obeahman murdered Cas's dad when Cas was 7, and since then, Cas has been researching and training to fight and kill the creature that killed his dad. <br>2) Anna, the dead luuuuuuuuurve of Cas's life, dragged the Obeahman out of the world at the end of book 1. <br>3) Anna then started to appear to Cas (shades of Edward in New Moon), because apparently cutting her with the athame one time linked her to it, and he decided to save her. <br>4) The "saving" involved Cas and Thomas and Carmel meeting the Order of the Black Dagger, who let Cas cross over to try to save her... where he does so, and ohyeahhisdadistheretoo. <br><br>Yes. His father, the murdered guy who helped bring Cas into being and who saved people from murderous spirits is relegated to a damn AFTERTHOUGHT!<br><br>WHY was saving his DAD not the plot, since we KNOW he is linked to the athame since it's been a bloodline weapon since page ONE. Why go in the "I have no meaning in my life without her" route? SHE IS DEAD ALREADY, and cursed or not, had killed dozens of people, and again, their "relationship" was only a period of months. There was no meaning there. Not like there is in a parent/child relationship. So shunting the "I do this to avenge my father" purpose to a fucking afterthought in favor of 200+ pages of whiny teen brooding is just... It's SO AGGRAVATING. <br><br>Just... whatever. I'm done here. <br><br><span>[image error]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="1828860714223426160" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2016726186590575439">I really love how it ended eventhough some bits were sluggish. My favorite part is the gang of course. I love the characterization and the bond they all formed. I have to say I really ship Carmel and Thomas. Carmel is a spitfire, I’ll 10/10 would support her. I feel a little bad because Jestine and Cas would loooook cute, their simmering tension. Yo, I’m here for that. I wish there’s a Jestine spin-off book or something. <br/><br/>Overall: I really love this series and I’m glad I gave it a chance.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yyJiDpBKSnpE0R6JR8n0guxyALjSN3kspP13101POVx8rrZrCPOBp5dAxpcvSGLwcZdEJOTuYmHArU9FqIfByA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/HP0X8oy01AdNfwcs2Ywm9M37XCmOAE++R3YKz6bu5RL/yA6UosYjc6kJALb56bpTtKp7JDhGnOdTeC521NDAA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer3602973050928349070">So, I write books. The Anna Dressed in Blood duo is horror, The Goddess War trilogy is mythology, and Three Dark Crowns is fantasy, because the world don't move to the beat of just one drum. What might be right for you, may not be right for some. Love to read, too.   <span id="freeText3602973050928349070" style="display:none">So, I write books. The Anna Dressed in Blood duo is horror, The Goddess War trilogy is mythology, and Three Dark Crowns is fantasy, because the world don't move to the beat of just one drum. What might be right for you, may not be right for some. Love to read, too. Fiction, philosophy, good books, bad books, because you take the good you take the bad you take them both and there you have a stack of books and stuff. I mean, you've got to be adventurous. There's more to life that what you're living, so take a chance and face the wind. <br /><br />There's more coming soon like ALL THESE BODIES and a new fantasy series, so don't waste another minute on your cryin. We're nowhere near the end. <br /><br />My likes include animals, food, and nostalgia. I mean, whatever happened to predictability? The milkman, the paperboy, the evening TV? Used to be everywhere you look, there's a heart, a hand to hold on to.<br /><br />Anyway, I love to hear from readers so drop me a line here or at my website and we'll talk about friends to know, and ways to grow, and how if you threw a party you would see that the biggest gift would be from me and the card attached would say, thank you for being a friend.<br /><br />We can also talk about all the sitcom theme songs in this bio. Sha la la la.</span>

Now, armed with his father\'s mysterious and deadly athame, Cas travels the country with his kitchen-witch mother and their spirit-sniffing cat. They follow legends and local lore, destroy the murderous dead, and keep pesky things like the future and friends at bay.\n\nSearching for a ghost the locals call Anna Dressed in Blood, Cas expects the usual: track, hunt, kill. What he finds instead is a girl entangled in curses and rage, a ghost like he\'s never faced before. She still wears the dress she wore on the day of her brutal murder in 1958: once white, now stained red and dripping with blood. Since her death, Anna has killed any and every person who has dared to step into the deserted Victorian she used to call home.\n\nYet she spares Cas\'s life.<\/span>\n  <a   <!--
This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
